New general textbooks on forensic psychology seem to emerge every few months. Therefore to get a more detailed, up-to-date 
overview of this rapidly developing field, it is best to seek out the most recent books. However, at the time of writing, the 
following can be recommended: C. R. Bartol and A. M. Bartol, [3mIntroduction to Forensic Psychology: Research and Application [0m
(London: Sage, 2008). 

D. Canter and D. Youngs, [3mInvestigative Psychology: Offender Profiling and the Analysis of Criminal Action [0m(Chichester: Wiley, 
2009). 

D. A. Crighton and G. J. Towl, [3mPsychology in Prisons [0m, 2nd edn. (Oxford: BPS Blackwell, 2008). 

D. Howitt, [3mIntroduction to Forensic and Criminal Psychology [0m(London: Prenice Hall, 2009). 

M. T. Huss, [3mForensic Psychology: Research, Clinical Practice, and Applications [0m(Chichester: Wiley-Blackwell, 2009). 

D. A. Kraus and J. D. Lieberman (eds.), [3mPsychological Expertise in Court [0m(Farnham: Ashgate, 2009). 

J. D. Lieberman and D. A. Kraus (eds.), [3mJury Psychology: Social Aspects of the Trial Process [0m(Farnham: Ashgate, 2009). 

A. Vrij, [3mDetecting Lies and Deceit: Pitfalls and Opportunities [0m(Chichester: Wiley, 2008).
